Swaine</a></span></section><nav class="prev-next-pagination margin-top-50 margin-bottom-50 grid no-gutter has-previous ">        <div class="pagination-control pagination-panel grid-xs has-link">                            <a href="/technology/computer/Introduction" class="previous grid no-gutter">                    <i class="material-icons md-36 grid-xs-shrink middle-xs" data-icon="keyboard_arrow_left"></i>                    <div class="grid-xs" data-layout="column">                        <small class="pagination-control-label text-uppercase">Previous page</small>                        <span class="pagination-control-description text-ellipsis" title="Introduction">Introduction</span>                    </div>                </a>                    </div>                    <div class="pagination-content pagination-panel grid-xs-shrink text-center text-uppercase">                Page 2 of 2            </div>                <div class="pagination-control pagination-panel text-right grid-xs ">                    </div>    </nav></article><div class="md-learn-more extra-content" data-module="learn-more" data-value="learn-more">        <h2>Learn More <span>in these related Britannica articles:</span></h2>        <ul>        <li class="entry">                <a href="/science/computer-science">                    <div class="image-wrapper text-center">                            				<img src="https://cdn.britannica.com/180x300/44/7744-004-5D8A5931.jpg"  alt="The basic organization of a computer." />	</div>                    <div class="title"><strong>computer science</strong></div>                    <div class="description"><e ty="b"><strong>Computer</strong> science</e>,  the study of computers, including their design (architecture) and their uses for computations, data processing, and systems control. In 1946 the first techniques of photocomposition were developed. With this method of typesetting, the images of pages are prepared for the printer photographically, as on a photocopier, instead of in lines…</div>                </a>            </li>        <li class="entry">                <a href="/art/history-of-the-motion-picture/The-war-years-and-post-World-War-II-trends#ref508310">                    <div class="image-wrapper text-center">                            				<img src="https://cdn.britannica.com/180x300/69/59669-004-C063A6A4.jpg"  alt="One photograph of a series taken by Eadweard Muybridge of a running horse." />	</div>                    <div class="title"><strong>history of the motion picture: The effect of new technologies</strong></div>                    <div class="description">…means of motion-picture distribution, and computer-generated graphics provided new means of production, especially of special effects, forecasting the prospect of a fully automated “electronic cinema.” Many studios, including Universal and Columbia, devoted the majority of their schedules to the production of telefilms for the commercial television networks, and nearly all…</div>                </a>            </li>        <li class="entry">                <a href="/technology/history-of-technology/The-20th-century#ref368122">                    <div class="image-wrapper text-center">                            				<img src="https://cdn.britannica.com/180x300/05/4605-004-87C6CE6F.jpg"  alt="Drawing of an Egyptian seagoing ship, c. 2600 bce based on vessels depicted in the bas-relief discovered in the pyramid of King Sahure at Abū Ṣīr, Cairo." />	</div>                    <div class="title"><strong>history of technology: Automation and the computer</strong></div>                    <div class="description">Both old and new materials were used increasingly in the engineering industry, which was transformed since the end of World War II by the introduction of control engineering, automation, and computerized techniques. The vital piece of equipment has been the computer, especially the electronic…</div>                </a>            </li>        </ul>    </div><div class="md-additional-media extra-content"><h2>ADDITIONAL MEDIA</h2><ul><li><figure data-type="image" class="md-assembly no-caption media-overlay-link print-false" data-assembly-id="19612"><div class="md-assembly-wrapper" data-type="image"><div class="image-wrapper mg"><img src="https://cdn.britannica.com/500x150/05/24405-004-F1EBC37C.jpg" big-src="https://cdn.britannica.com/05/24405-004-F1EBC37C.jpg" alt="Apple's Lisa computer" data-width="422" data-height="300"></div></div></figure></li><li><figure data-type="image" class="md-assembly no-caption media-overlay-link print-false" data-assembly-id="94239"><div class="md-assembly-wrapper" data-type="image"><div class="image-wrapper mg"><img src="https://cdn.britannica.com/500x150/03/24403-004-E0CA7D37.jpg" big-src="https://cdn.britannica.com/03/24403-004-E0CA7D37.jpg" alt="The first Apple computer." data-width="452" data-height="300"></div></div></figure></li><li><figure data-type="image" class="md-assembly no-caption media-overlay-link print-false" data-assembly-id="132976"><div class="md-assembly-wrapper" data-type="image"><div class="image-wrapper mg"><img src="https://cdn.britannica.com/500x150/91/79391-004-EE7354D6.jpg" big-src="https://cdn.britannica.com/91/79391-004-EE7354D6.jpg" alt="A detail of the Intel Desktop Board D915GUX. You can make it easier for us to review and, hopefully, publish your contribution by keeping a few points in mind.        </p>        <ol>            <li>Encyclop&aelig;dia Britannica articles are written in a neutral objective tone for a general audience.</li>            <li>You may find it helpful to search within the site to see how similar or related subjects are covered.</li>            <li>Any text you add should be original, not copied from other sources.</li>            <li>At the bottom of the article, feel free to list any sources that support your changes, so that we can fully understand their context. (Internet URLs are the best.)</li>        </ol>        <p>            Your contribution may be further edited by our staff, and its publication is subject to our final approval. Unfortunately, our editorial approach may not be able to accommodate all contributions.        </p>    </div></div><div id="md-edit-leave" class="md-edit-mode-modal ui-hidden">    <div class="md-modal-header">        <div class="md-modal-title md-heading-3"></div>    </div>    <div class="md-modal-body text-center">        <div class="md-modal-message"></div>        <div class="text-center">            <button class="md-leave md-button md-link"></button>            <button class="md-submit md-button md-primary">Submit</button>        </div>    </div></div><div id="md-edit-confirmation" class="md-edit-mode-modal ui-hidden">    <div class="md-modal-header">        <div class="md-modal-title md-heading-3">Thank You for Your Contribution!</div>    </div>    <div class="md-modal-body">        <p>Our editors will review what you've submitted, and if it meets our criteria, we'll add it to the article.</p>        <p>Please note that our editors may make some formatting changes or correct spelling or grammatical errors, and may also contact you if any clarifications are needed.</p>        <div class="text-center">            <button class="md-button md-primary"></button>        </div>    </div></div><div id="md-edit-error" class="md-edit-mode-modal ui-hidden">    <div class="md-modal-header">        <div class="md-modal-title md-heading-3">Uh Oh</div>    </div>    <div class="md-modal-body text-center">        <p>There was a problem with your submission.
